99	where did francisco coronado come from	  Francisco Coronado was born in Salamanca, Spain in 1510. He came from a family of noble background and was well-educated. He sailed to the New World in 1535 and eventually made his way to Mexico, where he became a successful conquistador. In 1540, he set out on an expedition to explore the American Southwest in search of the legendary Seven Cities of Gold. He and his men traveled through present-day Arizona, New Mexico, and Texas before finally turning back in 1542. Although they never found the fabled cities, Coronado's expedition was one of the most significant in terms of opening up the American West to European exploration.

400	who were mary shelley	  The author of Frankenstein, Mary Shelley was born in 1797. Mary Shelley grew up in a household of intellectual and political radicals, and she was exposed to some of the most important ideas of her time from an early age. This environment shaped her own thinking on many issues, including the role of women in society. In 1814, she met the poet Percy Bysshe Shelley, and they eloped the following year. The couple were married in 1816, and Mary Shelley gave birth to their first child, a daughter, in 1817. The couple had two more children, a son and a daughter, but both died in infancy. Mary Shelley's husband Percy Bysshe Shelley died in 1822, leaving her a widow at the age of 25. Mary Shelley continued to write and publish throughout her life, although she is best remembered for her novel Frankenstein, which was published in 1818.

975	what form of government does australia use	  Australia is a constitutional monarchy with a parliamentary democracy. The Queen of Australia is the head of state, and the Prime Minister of Australia is the head of government. The Queen is represented in Australia by the Governor-General, who is appointed by the Queen on the advice of the Prime Minister.  The Australian Parliament is bicameral, consisting of the House of Representatives and the Senate. The House of Representatives is elected by the people of Australia, and the Senate is elected by the people of the states and territories of Australia. The Parliament of Australia has the power to make laws for the peace, order, and good government of Australia.  The Australian Constitution is the supreme law of Australia. The Constitution establishes the framework of the Australian federal system, and sets out the powers and functions of the Commonwealth government.  The Constitution was drafted at a series of constitutional conventions held in the 1890s. It was ratified by the people of Australia in a series of referendums held in 1898 and 1899. The Constitution came into effect on 1 January 1901, when the six colonies of Australia federated to form the Commonwealth of Australia.

1010	what was john tyler	  John Tyler was the tenth president of the United States. He was elected vice president on the Whig ticket in 1840, and became president after the death of William Henry Harrison in 1841. Tyler was a staunch advocate of states' rights, and his administration was marked by a series of vetoes of bills from the Whig-controlled Congress. He was eventually expelled from the party, and ran for reelection as an independent in 1844. He was defeated in a landslide, and retired from public life.

1014	where was the boston tea party 1773	  The Boston Tea Party was a political and mercantile protest by the Sons of Liberty in Boston, Massachusetts, on December 16, 1773. The target was the Tea Act of May 10, 1773, which allowed the British East India Company to sell tea from China in American colonies without paying taxes apart from those imposed by the Townshend Acts. American Patriots strongly opposed the taxes in the tea as they believed that it violated their rights as Englishmen to be taxed only by their own elected representatives.

2244	what did the scientist thomson discover	  Thomson discovered the electron in 1897. He did so by using a cathode ray tube, which is a tube that contains a gas and two metal plates. When electricity is applied to the gas, it produces a beam of electrons. Thomson observed that the electrons were attracted to the positive plate and repelled by the negative plate. He also found that the electrons were deflected by a magnetic field. From these observations, Thomson concluded that the electrons were tiny particles with a negative charge.

3031	what is the political system of nigeria	  Nigeria is a federal republic with a presidential system of government. The president is the head of state and head of government, and is elected by popular vote for a four-year term. The president is the commander-in-chief of the armed forces and has the power to appoint and dismiss the prime minister and other members of the cabinet. The president is also responsible for appointing the chief justice and other members of the judiciary.  The National Assembly is the legislature of Nigeria and is made up of the Senate and the House of Representatives. The Senate is the upper house and is made up of three senators from each state and one from the Federal Capital Territory. The House of Representatives is the lower house and is made up of 360 members, who are elected by popular vote to serve four-year terms.  The Nigerian constitution provides for a system of checks and balances, whereby the executive branch is accountable to the legislature and the judiciary is independent of both the executive and the legislature.  Nigeria has a multi-party system, with two major political parties, the All Progressives Congress and the Peoples Democratic Party.

4353	what government does france have	  The French government is a unitary semi-presidential republic. The government is composed of the executive branch, the legislative branch, and the judicial branch.  The executive branch is headed by the President of the Republic, who is elected by the people. The President appoints the Prime Minister, who is the head of the government. The Prime Minister and the other members of the government make up the Council of Ministers.  The legislative branch is composed of the National Assembly and the Senate. The National Assembly is elected by the people and has the power to pass laws. The Senate is composed of representatives of the regions of France and has the power to veto laws passed by the National Assembly.  The judicial branch is composed of the Constitutional Court, the Supreme Court, and the lower courts. The Constitutional Court is responsible for ensuring that laws are in line with the Constitution. The Supreme Court is the highest court in the land and is responsible for hearing appeals from lower courts.

4505	what form of government does australia	  Australia is a federal parliamentary democracy and a constitutional monarchy. The Queen of Australia is the head of state, and the Prime Minister of Australia is the head of government.  The Australian Constitution establishes a system of government based on the principles of separation of powers, federalism, and representative democracy. The Constitution divides power between the federal government and the state and territory governments.  The federal government is responsible for matters that affect the whole of Australia, such as defense, foreign affairs, trade, and immigration. The state and territory governments are responsible for matters that affect their respective jurisdictions, such as education, health, and transport.  The Parliament of Australia is the legislative branch of the federal government. It is composed of the House of Representatives and the Senate. The House of Representatives is elected by the people of Australia, and the Senate is elected by the people of the states and territories.  The judicial branch of the federal government is the High Court of Australia. The High Court is the highest court in the land, and its decisions are binding on all other courts in Australia.

The construction of the Pyramids: The Pyramids are some of the most iconic structures in the world and were built during the Old Kingdom period of Egyptian history. They served as both tombs for the Pharaohs and as grandiose displays of the wealth and power of the Egyptian state.  3. The reign of Tutankhamun: Tutankhamun was one of the most famous Pharaohs in Egyptian history, due in large part to the discovery of his tomb by Howard Carter in 1922. His tomb was packed with incredible treasures, which have given us a great deal of insight into the life and times of this ancient Egyptian ruler.  4. The conquest of Egypt by Alexander the Great: In 332 BCE, Alexander the Great invaded and conquered Egypt. This was a significant event in Egyptian history as it marked the end of the native Egyptian dynasties and the beginning of Greek rule.  5. The construction of the temple of Karnak: The temple of Karnak is one of the largest and most impressive religious complexes in the world. It was constructed over a period of centuries and reached its height of grandeur during the New Kingdom period of Egyptian history.
